< Review>
This place is what you could describe as super chill hangout. It's nestled nicely in the community of Grand Terrace, right off the 215 freeway. I took a friend from New Jersey, after work, and he loved it, as well as I. The selections included IPA's, sours and stouts. As well a variety of bottled and canned beers. They will have more than enough to wet your palate. Swing by and enjoy, night or day. We went on a Monday and sat under a heat lamp till 10pm, trust, enjoy. Cheers friends.  üëçüòâüî•üçªüç∫</Review>

Hidden gem ! Really like the hidden tucked in the back feel of this place. <GmapID>0x80dcac4c800f7a6d:0x4ef97f93eb62a033</GmapID>< text>
This little place is hard to find. No kidding, we've literally, after having been there before, driven past it on several occasions trying to pick the right drive way to turn into. The tap list rotates often and is always interesting. It's a good thing I don't live closer or I'd spend way more time here. Staff is very knowledgeable and genial. The bottle list is impressive and pretty extensive as well. They allow smoking on the patio, which is a negative for me, but we've never had much trouble getting a seat inside if we want it. You can bring food in. A bonus is what I believe to be the world's best Domino's pizza, equally invisible up front in the same parking lot. Get a beer, order a cheap pizza that is surprisingly good, and then chow it fresh out of the oven at your table. This is a total winner.</text>

<gmap_id>0x80c2b546b53b7b21:0x5759b6727efad7e0<//gmap_id>< review>
My dog, Chelsea, had knee surgery replacement on both of her hind legs at a different veterinarian in November of 2020. Unfortunately, in late December of the same year, she fell while I was taking her out to do her deeds and she broke her right hind leg. My dog was crying and shaking. I simply could not drive all the way to the initial veterinarian to take care of my dog.

I Yelped full-service veterinarians in the Los Angeles area and found Economico Animal Hospital had 5-star reviews. After reading the reviews and the stories, I decided this was the place to take Chelsea.

Dr. Hwang conducted his veterinarian assessment and was very honest about the procedures, costs and realistic expectations about Chelsea's ability to be able to utilize that hind leg at 100%. He also mentioned the possibility of amputation if the situation got worst. He was caring, honest and his bed side manners where on point. He also tried to accommodate the cost since he knew I had already spent an arm and a leg on Chelsea's prior surgery. I agreed to the treatment and Chelsea ended up getting a metal piece on her hind leg to help strengthen the broken bone area. The healing process has been long but worth it.

As of January 22, 2021, Chelsea is now able to fully walk on her four legs and she is as happy and active as before. The only difference is that when she runs, she sometimes hops. I think it's because the metal on her leg doesn't allow her to coordinate her legs as before. But I take that any day over a leg amputation or her limping. She is doing amazing.  Dr. Hwang is a kind, caring miracle worker.

Please note that although they have tons of customers, they process their customers fairly quickly. All of their staff is caring, loving and honest. You will not be disappointed by their prices and specially their great quality. Can't thank them enough for their work and dedication.< /review>

<rate>2<//rate><review>While I'm sure it is not the most expensive for teeth cleaning/extractions out there, it is still expensive for an average animal hospital. I got quoted/ they were going to charge me a little over $1,000 to get my dog's  teeth cleaned and to do "major" extractions. They claimed extractions were necessary, but I would like to point out that they didn't specify what teeth needed to come out or how they came to that conclusion. In addition, I needed to update my dogs vaccines, so that was also included in the quote. I get it, performing extractions is more involved which should be more expensive. But listen, if you're going to charge for additional treatment (laser therapy), and then a bunch of other stuff (e.g. Elizabeth collar, anesthesia monitoring, anesthesia, pre anesthesia sedation, anesthesia induction, clindamycin injection, ketoprofen injection, oral spray, different kinds of antibiotics) without offering alternatives, options, or even explanations I will start to question how reasonable those charges are. I am not a vet so I don't know how necessary each thing was, but an Ecollar/Elizabet collar?

I declined the dental stuff, but because I had already invested the time there I decided to just get my dog's vaccines updated. This included a 6 month bordetella, a 3 year rabies vaccination, a corona vaccination, and a canine DHPP. Other than the rabbies vaccine, all were $22.00. The rabbies was $15.00. They charged a $5.00 biohazard waste fee. They did give me a $20.00 discount. My total was $66.00. Also, I did not ask for, nor was I asked if I wanted my dog to receive a corona vaccine which from my understanding is not usually recommended. Bordetella, and rabies were the only ones I mentioned to the vet, but they proceeded with the other two without telling me. Some may know that a rabbies shot can be given for as low as $10.00. A bordetella is usually around $20.00. I'm not sure about the other two.

Again, while not the most expensive vet there is, I don't think it is very "economical", and I question their treatment recommendations. Later in the day, I called other vets and got quoted for half the price for my dog's dental work.

The staff and vet were friendly enough which is why I gave them an extra star.

I hope this helps narrow someone's search for a good vetinarian.< /review><username>Stephanie Fierro</username>< gmapID>

<Name>AnitaBonghit 69</Name>< text>
I have mixed feelings about my visit so I'll write an honest review. I brought my old car here before for tint and there was bubbles so I knew not to go here for tint again and thought they couldn't possibly mess up a subwoofer. The guys who installed my amp and sub did a great job, especially considering I showed up with a car full of junk on a Friday afternoon. It sounds okay too, after some adjustments. The thing is, I specifically asked for 1000 watts. Half way home after picking up, I knew something was wrong. I had a 500 watt amp and two 250 watt subs instead of the 1000 watts that I repeatedly asked for, but they were closed. The next day the salesman I dealt with insisted that a 500 watt amp and two subs that can handle that 500 watts IS a "1000 watt system". I was shocked because I've installed systems in all my cars and dealt with music equipment for as long as I can remember and this is not a thing. A guitar speaker cabinet and head unit, for example, would be advertised as 200 watts because it is 200 watts of power, not a 100 watt head and four 25 watt speakers. I get that the speakers can handle that divided power, but nobody adds the watts the amp outputs with the watts the speakers can handle and calls it whatever the outcome of that equation happens to be. I called around to other audio shops and nobody does that. The dude played me. If I knew I would be getting half the power I would have done it myself for so much cheaper. He told me it would be 300$ more to upgrade to the system I want and that my old 1000 watt amp was weaker. The ease and straight face with which he told me that I have a "1000 watt system" with a 500 watt amp makes me think this is what he does regularly. I encourage everyone who brought their vehicle here to check exactly what was installed, as some others may not be as electronically inclined and susceptible to being taken advantage of. I also encourage future customers to be thoroughly verbal with the salesman in order to prevent this. Although, I thought I was thorough, considering I specifically asked for 1000 watts many times. Just beware and be aware.</text>
